< text>
If you're desperate for Korean food then by all means go to this place and it'll get you by.  But don't expect this place to blow you out of the water for Korean food experience. Kimchi was so sour it belongs in the liquor cabinet.  Bibimbop was sour and sweet. The $50 galbi was 70% bones and ended up being about $4 per piece.  Perhaps I'm spoiled by Oakland, but I've had better Korean in Chicago suburbs than this place.</text>

<username>Anne Casillas< /username><Date>1513869775886<//Date><rating>5< /rating>< Text>
11-22-2015, Wow this place is GREAT, the owners are super nice and the food very tasty.  We had the Beef Kalbi and Daeji Bulugogi.  Both meat dishes were done to perfection.  If you like hot food be sure to tell them, they will put the real Korean heat to it, otherwise its going to be a nice medium hot for most novices. Sides were numerous and the kimchi full of tangy fermented goodness. The leek potato pancakes are lovely. But the homemade Korean donuts warmly rolled in sugar, were too wonderful to resist!  Prices compare to any other Korean BBQ in south San Jose and the friendly owners were definitely a bonus you don't find often. Can't wait to go back!<//Text>

<Date>1622232203883</Date>< Text>
Came here for lunch bc we could walk here. Spectacular, well made food, and you can tell they put thought into making their recipes special! I'd been wanting to stop by for a while but the stars never aligned for a trip until today. Will absolutely be back.

I had the Piggly Wiggly, ham w spicy sauce on baguette, which was delicious - perfect spice level imo. For reference, I prefer "spicy" level kimchi and put Frank's Red Hot on my pizza for added saltiness.

Husband had turkey and avocado. He said it was better than the last place we had sandwiches from, and noted the bread was crusty, had some pep (maybe horseradish, he couldn't remember ingredients) to it.

Covid safe (workers wearing mask + face shield, take out only with order at the door, wiped down payment register bt customers, CC only), and the people inside were very nice. It was $22.50 for two sandwiches and one bag of chips.</Text>

< Text>
The sandwiches were really good and a good size portion. They use good bread and good ingredients and it makes a big difference. We had the roast beef and wicked piggy, both of which were very good. The horseradish cream and Sriracha cream cheese made the sandwiches. The guy (I think an owner) was super nice and gave me a free cup of coffee to try (it was strong but not too overpowering or burnt) and mentioned they have a shop in Oakland too. The inside is small so it's more of a take out place, but there is a small counter that could fit 4 or 5 people and some tables outside. I'll definitely go back.</Text>

<Review>Superb sandwiches, strong (as advertised) coffee. Both staffers are engaged with customers, activity soliciting (and taking!) feedback from the customers of this new coffee/sandwich shop.

A few things stood out to me, first - the good:

They have a free library! A few small bookcases filled with a rather eclectic selection of books. I asked, and the books are free to read - and take with you! The "take with you" part is on an honor system that you will either return it or replace it with a different book.

Among other things, I suggested that they add a squeeze  bottle of simple sugar to their cream/sugar/etc bar of additions for drinks - as it's the best way to sweeten cold drinks. They agreed - and pointed to a white board where "add simple syrup" (to coffee condiments) as already on their "To Do" list. But they went beyond that and offered to make up a bit - on the spot - so I could sweeten my cold pressed iced coffee (as I'd already added sugar and stirred vigorously, I declined)!

They also were quite interested in my suggestion to get their pastries from Starter bakery. Currently, they're using City Bakery (the same ones Peet's uses), but should business allow (they are, after all, a startup), they plan on switching to a premium bakery - and noted my preference.

The bad:

Nothing actually bad about my experience, but I see two obstacles to long term success of this startup: Parking and Seating.

Parking: Cafe N!ne is one of a number of storefront businesses that share this corner mall. While the mall has a parking lot, far too many of the spaces were marked as "Reserved for Bank of the West" resulting in almost no parking available for the rest of the businesses. As I sat in their outdoor seating area consuming my delicious cold brew and ham sandwich, I observed no fewer than 5 cars waiting patiently for a non-bank space to open. This doesn't bode well for future visits.

Seating: It's lacking. There is a 4 seat counter across from the cash register, and seating for another 12-15 people outside. Should their business attract the customer base that their coffee and sandwiches deserves, seating will be hard to find - impossible in cold/windy weather.

I didn't ding any stars for these negatives. Cafe N!ne is a startup, likely on a limited budget. I'm betting they took the space because they can afford it. Hopefully, they do well enough to move to someplace nearby without the negatives I've mentioned. I hope they succeed.<//Review><rate>5< /rate><pictures>None< /pictures><user_id>111524681621264503243< /user_id><gmapID>0x808578ff871c34bd:0x55cfbd0fb15fe562</gmapID><Time>1512688874302<//Time><user_name>Steven Dorst< /user_name></record>

<Text>When I first moved here this was one of the major downtown SF shopping stops. With all of the high-end designer stores and small,but well known up and coming stores all in one short walk from one another. < Review>
A Beverly Hills institution. I‚Äôm glad to see that they aren‚Äôt closed post-covid so one could still enjoy some tasty pastrami. You can order ahead online or via phone. You can specify a pick up time online, but if you try to specify a time over the phone, it doesn‚Äôt work. Our sandwiches seemed to have been sitting for a while, but the pastrami was still delicious (albeit the bread was a tad soggy). Credit cards are accepted. Street parking.

The New Yorker with the coleslaw and Russian dressing is my go-to. The thick cut pastrami is so deliciously fatty and the creaminess of the dressing complements it well. If you like mustard, it adds some needed acidity as you progress into the sandwich. You get an option of a side, and I typically go for the macaroni salad. On my most recent pick up, the sides were missing but at least the pickles were there. You can pick the type of bread, but the standard is double baked rye. You‚Äôll probably enter a food coma if you eat both sandwiches, but it‚Äôs well worth it.</Review>

<text>This is my first stop in Beverly Hills when I arrive in the USA. As a person who lived in NYC I can really say what pastrami is, how it has to taste and how pastrami must be. I am maybe one of the only persons on the planet who made his own pastrami day and went to 11 (!!!!) of the most famous pastrami places in nyc. < text>
This is my first stop in Beverly Hills when I arrive in the USA. As a person who lived in NYC I can really say what pastrami is, how it has to taste and how pastrami must be. I am maybe one of the only persons on the planet who made his own pastrami day and went to 11 (!!!!) of the most famous pastrami places in nyc. In ONE DAY! if someone on this planet would have told me that the pastrami place in Beverly Hills is beating Katz's, Ben's Best and Artie's - I would have never believed him. But it is true. Nate and Al is not fancy because it is in Beverly Hills. It is the best because they offer the best pastrami on planet earth, authentic location, extremely nice service and fair pricing. This was my first time at Nate'n Al. My friend and her mother who brought me there had both been going since they were little children. Since it was my first time there, I got the signature Nate'n Al sandwich, which is hot pastrami, tomato, lettuce, and Russian dressing. I got it on rye with a side of cole slaw and a cup of matzo ball soup. Everything was really good. Also the pickles are fantastic! My friend says you can tell a lot from a person based on whether they prefer the old or new dills. They were both awesome (I'm partial to the old ones - they pack a punch!). The space is vibrant, has a lot of history, and apparently it's not uncommon to run into celebs.<//Review>

<text>One street over from world famous Rodeo drive is a LA institution, the closest you will get to NYC on the West Coast: Nate'n Al.

This little place has been serving up the good since the 1940's and is a fantastic choice for breakfast or lunch. They say that several A-Listers come to the spot frequently including Larry King, but you may not recognize them in a hat and glasses.

On a recent visit we found a 20 minute wait and opted to sit outside. The waitress was friendly and attentive, while the host got us our drinks. Coke comes in a can here, the old fashion way.

The omelet was incredible, as was the onion bagel.  Prices were fair to average. Portions were fine. Coffee came quick and so did the refills. We were treated right, and tried our best not to stand out as tourists as it was obvious that most of the people were were locals or regulars.

Down to the pickles and sandwiches this place was 100% authentic NYC style Jewish deli. I can't wait to go back.</text>< pics>
None< /pics>

< Text>
One street over from world famous Rodeo drive is a LA institution, the closest you will get to NYC on the West Coast: Nate'n Al.

This little place has been serving up the good since the 1940's and is a fantastic choice for breakfast or lunch. They say that several A-Listers come to the spot frequently including Larry King, but you may not recognize them in a hat and glasses.

On a recent visit we found a 20 minute wait and opted to sit outside. The waitress was friendly and attentive, while the host got us our drinks. Coke comes in a can here, the old fashion way.

The omelet was incredible, as was the onion bagel.  Prices were fair to average. Portions were fine. Coffee came quick and so did the refills. We were treated right, and tried our best not to stand out as tourists as it was obvious that most of the people were were locals or regulars.

Down to the pickles and sandwiches this place was 100% authentic NYC style Jewish deli. I can't wait to go back.</Text>

<user_name>Jeanne Phillips<//user_name>< text>
My husband And I had dinner at N & A last night. After we were seated a busboy brought us water. I
A half hour later the server finally came to take our order which was two omelets. It took another half hour for the food to arrive. It was very average. I ordered a second cup of coffee. The server forgot to bring it until he passed by more than an hour later and I reminded him. The empty dishes remained on our table for about an hour after that, until I cleared the table for myself and the other couple we were with. They thought it was amusing, but I was tired at looking at the dirty dishes.
I will never returned to that restaurant again. The omelets are better at IHOP and so is the service.< /text>

< Review>
LOVE THIS PLACE!!!!!!!
I  used to get my hair done a few blocks away and they ordered from here and offered me a sandwich one day and I declined  because (A)... I'm not much of a tuna eater and (B) ... I do not like a lot of meat of any kind  in a sandwich and that sandwich needed it's own thickness zip code (C) ... I'm not a deli eater I never ate at one before. So that right there's 3 good  reasons why I was not interested. "HOWEVER" when I declined the entire place of about 20+ people all got quiet and they looked at me as if I committed some crime then someone said... "Have you ever had Nate N Al's before?'' I replied "No". Well lets just say I caused somewhat of a mini riot and  was completely given the run down on why never to refuse a Nate N Al's " sandwich.  UGH ...OK OK ! I said and took the sandwich to shut everyone up basically . At this point you can hear a needle drop as they all were looking at me I was given a Tuna sandwich and I thought this is not gonna end well and they're all gonna send me into a cornfield cause I know I'm not going to like it.  So I held my breath  and reluctantly bit the sandwich  and everything I thought in my A.B.C the 3 reasons why not to just flew out the window and everything I once believed died just like that right there!  I mean wow  I just bit into the best freaking sandwich I've ever had in my LIFE EVER ... YES MY ENTIRE LIFE!!!!!!!!!!!  So the next day I went to pick up my mom and told her we're going to have tuna sandwiches at Nate N Al's for lunch and she thought I went crazy and  said Tuna sandwiches, Why would I want a tuna sandwich?
"Mom this time you have to just go long with me  you know I'm a picky eater so it will be good I promise and for good measure  I picked up my 20 year old daughter who thought me and my mom both went crazy .Needless to say I ordered all our food 3 tuna sandwich plates and a soon as they bit into theirs they looked at me with big eyes and said OMG THIS IS SO FREAKING GOOD yeah both of them along with saying it was the best sandwich they ever had in their lives. I'm not sure how they do it but you can't replicate that sandwich!
I HIGHLY RECOMMEND THIS PLACE AND TRY THE TUNA IF YOUR NOT ALLERGIC YOU WILL BECOME A FAN! THANKS NATE N AL'S YOU PEOPLE KILLED IT BEST SANDWICH ON THE PLANET EVER  MADE PERIOD!!!!!!!<//Review>

<time>1475433551219<//time><Rating>3</Rating><Review>A solid, if not touristy, Jewish style deli in the heart of Beverly Hills.

An overwhelmingly extensive menu of all the best Jewish style foods... chicken soup with matzo balls or kreplach, smoked fish and bagels, liver, pastrami, etc. And the pickles! I just want plates and plates of them.

The appetizer platters seem to be the way to go. Alone they are tons of food.. the fish of your choice served with tomato, onion, lettuce, cream cheese, and bagel. Their fish was great for an offering outside of NY.

I found the latkes disappointing, boiled potatoes instead of shredded, and not enough onion. Too thick, not crispy. But served properly with your choice of apple sauce and/or sour cream. The chicken soup had humongous matzo balls but came with pasta instead of vegetables or chicken, and definitely needed salt and pepper.

I'll have to come back to try the sandwiches!</Review>< pics>

< Text>
a classic since 1945. old school deli with to-go counter and large dine-in restaurant. bagels, lox, schmears, soft, double-baked rye bread, pumpernickel, corned beef, brisket, pastrami, cole slaw, knishes, potato pancakes, blintzes, ruggula, Dr. Brown's sodas, breakfast, lunch, dinner, meal and sandwich combos galore. Everything fresh, everything nostalgic of old NY delis of the bygone era, ys, Nate and Al's has outlived the Carnegie Deli and so many others, and it's still going strong in the heart of Beverly Hills.< /Text>

< Rate>
3<//Rate>
< Text>
They offer a fresh and tasty reuben in the standard corned beef or pastrami varieties (I split half of each with my nephew, since the only half-n-half they offer is stacked, not separated), but I felt that it fell far short of the online hype it enjoys.  For a "celebrated" delicatessen, I was rather disappointed.  It was good, but not fantastic.  The size of the stacking was equally unimpressive.  A regular corned beef sandwich I saw go by was much more generously stacked.  It was my first experience here, so perhaps this was a fluke, but I have to go by what I'm given and, although the service was good, I won't bother returning for another reuben.  Rather underwhelming in general.< /Text>
